Impact of weather events on health and the US economy
========================================================

This is a report demonstrating the impact of severe weather events on population health and the economy at large in the USA. The *Storm Data* we explore is provided by the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) as a series of measurements taken between the year 1950 and November 2011.

# Loading the dataset


```r
download.file("https://d396qusza40orc.cloudfront.net/repdata%2Fdata%2FStormData.csv.bz2", 
    destfile = "StormData.csv.bz2", method = "curl")
data <- read.csv(bzfile("StormData.csv.bz2"), stringsAsFactors = FALSE)
```


# Question 1
Across the United States, which types of events (as indicated in the EVTYPE variable) are most harmful with respect to population health?

# Preprocessing 

It seems we have several timezones
I would be
How dirty is the Hour/minute part?


```r
unique(data$BGN_TIME)
```


 - odd use of military time jointly with AM/PM suffix
 - errors such as "1990", "2090", "2400", "9999", "000", "0572", "1580", "13O0" 


We will use a regexp to reformat them.


```r
unique(data$BGN_DATE)
```

```r
e <- data.frame()
for (tz in unique(data$TIME_ZONE)) {
    d <- subset(data, data$TIME_ZONE == tz)
    d$BGN_DATETIME <- as.Date(paste(d$BGN_DATE, " ", d$BGN_TIME), format = "%m/%d/%Y 0:00:00 %H%M", 
        tz = tz)
    e <- rbind(d, e)
}
data$BGN_DATE <- as.Date(data$BGN_DATE, format = "%m/%d/%Y 0:00:00")
```
